2:21:1071:0:14:72:515:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:How Much of Chinese Exports is Really Made In China? Assessing Domestic Value-Added
2:22:1154:14:14:72:247:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:When Processing Trade is Pervasive
2:23:1188:14:14:72:307:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Robert Koopman, Zhi Wang, and Shang-Jin Wei
2:24:1231:14:14:72:234:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 14109
2:25:1259:14:14:72:244:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:June 2008, Revised December 2011

2:27:1308:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:28:1316:28:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:The rise of China in world trade has brought both benefits and anxiety to other economies. For many
2:29:1415:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:policy questions, it is crucial to know the extent of domestic value added (DVA) in exports, but the
2:30:1515:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:computation is more complicated when processing trade is pervasive. We propose a method for computing
2:31:1616:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:domestic and foreign contents that allows for processing trade. By our estimation, the share of domestic
2:32:1720:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:content in exports by the PRC was about 50% before China’s WTO membership, and has risen to
2:33:1811:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:over 60% since then. There are also interesting variations across sectors. Those sectors that are likely
2:34:1915:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:labeled as relatively sophisticated such as electronic devices have particularly low domestic content
2:35:2016:14:42:72:169:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:(about 30% or less).
2:36:2036:42:14:72:155:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Robert Koopman
2:37:2050:14:14:72:160:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Research Division

3:58:2451:0:20:90:170:708:144:Times:144:Times:1. Introduction 
3:59:2467:20:21:90:93:688:144:Times:144:Times: 
3:60:2467:21:20:90:525:667:144:Times:144:Times:“Made in China” is one of the most common labels one encounters in a shopping mall in 
3:61:2552:20:21:90:528:647:144:Times:144:Times:the  United  States  and  Europe.  Increasingly,  many  products  that  are  supposed  to  be  
3:62:2647:21:21:90:521:626:144:Times:144:Times:technically  sophisticated  and  therefore  likely  to  be  associated  with  exports  from  high-
3:63:2745:21:21:90:525:605:144:Times:144:Times:income countries, such as digital cameras and computers, also carry that label. Since the 
3:64:2835:21:20:90:525:584:144:Times:144:Times:most salient characteristic of the factor endowment in China is a vast supply of unskilled 
3:65:2926:20:21:90:525:564:144:Times:144:Times:labor relative to either physical or human capital, is the country’s actual export structure 
3:66:3019:21:21:90:529:543:144:Times:144:Times:inconsistent  with  the  predictions  from  the  international  trade  theory  based  on  its  
3:67:3114:21:20:90:525:522:144:Times:144:Times:endowment?  A possible resolution to the puzzle is that China is simply the last section of 
3:68:3206:20:21:90:529:502:144:Times:144:Times:a  long  global  production  chain  that  ends  up  assembling  components  from  various  
3:69:3297:21:21:90:524:481:144:Times:144:Times:countries  into  a  final  product  before  it  is  exported  to  the  US  and  EU  market.  Indeed,  a 
3:70:3401:21:20:90:526:460:144:Times:144:Times:MacBook  computer  carries  a  label  at  its  back  (in  small  type)  that  reads  “Designed  by  
3:71:3501:20:21:90:527:440:144:Times:144:Times:Apple in  California;  Assembled  in  China.” This  label  is  likely  to  be  oversimplified  
3:72:3596:21:21:90:525:419:144:Times:144:Times:already, as  it  reports  only  the  head  and  the  tail  of  a  global production  chain,  but  skips 
3:73:3700:21:21:90:460:398:144:Times:144:Times:many other countries that supply other components that go into the product.  
3:74:3777:21:20:126:525:377:144:Times:144:Times:China is the archetype of a national economy that is well integrated into a global 
3:75:3860:20:21:90:526:357:144:Times:144:Times:production  chain.  It  imports  raw  material,  equipment,  and  intermediate  inputs,  and  then  
3:76:3960:21:21:90:526:336:144:Times:144:Times:exports  a  big  fraction  of  its  output  (on  the  order  of  37%  of  GDP  in  2006) to  the  world  
3:77:4065:21:20:90:525:315:144:Times:144:Times:market. The  PRC  is  not  the  only  country  whose  production  and  exports  are  a  part  of  a 
3:78:4164:20:21:90:529:295:144:Times:144:Times:global  chain;  Japan,  Korea,  Singapore,  and Malaysia  are  some  other  examples  of  
3:79:4254:21:21:90:525:274:144:Times:144:Times:countries  that  participate  actively in  the  international  divisions  of  labor.  However,  the 
3:80:4354:21:20:90:526:253:144:Times:144:Times:PRC is  noteworthy  due  to  its  sheer  size.  In  addition,  its  export/GDP  ratio,  at  35%  or  
3:81:4455:20:21:90:525:233:144:Times:144:Times:higher in recent years, is extraordinarily high for a large economy, when compared with 
3:82:4543:21:21:90:525:212:144:Times:144:Times:8% for the US and 13% for India. With a reputation as a “world factory,” China is a top 
3:83:4631:21:21:90:417:191:144:Times:144:Times:supplier of manufacturing outsourcing for many global companies.  
3:84:4697:21:20:126:525:170:144:Times:144:Times:For many policy issues, it is important to assess the extent of domestic content in 
3:85:4781:20:21:90:525:150:144:Times:144:Times:exports. For  example, what  is  the  effect  of  a  currency  appreciation  on  a  country’s 
3:86:4875:21:21:90:526:129:144:Times:144:Times:exports?  The  answer  depends  crucially  on  the  share  of  domestic  content  in  the  exports.  
3:87:4976:21:20:90:526:108:144:Times:144:Times:Other  things  being equal,  the  lower  the  share  of  domestic  content  in  the  exports,  the  
3:88:5076:20:0:90:524:88:144:Times:144:Times:smaller  the  effect  on  trade  volume  a  given  exchange  rate  appreciation  would  have.   As 
4:89:5177:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:another  example,  what  is  the  effect  of  trading  with  the  PRC  on  US  income  inequality?  
4:90:5277:21:21:90:528:688:144:Times:144:Times:The  answer  depends  in  part  on  whether  the  PRC  simply  exports  products  that  are  
4:91:5370:21:20:90:527:667:144:Times:144:Times:intensive  in  low-skilled  labor  or  whether  its  exports  are  more  sophisticated.  Rodrik  
4:92:5467:20:21:90:525:647:144:Times:144:Times:(2006) notes that the per capita income typically associated with the kind of goods bundle 
4:93:5558:21:21:90:525:626:144:Times:144:Times:that the PRC exports is much higher than the country’s actual income. He interprets this 
4:94:5647:21:21:90:527:605:144:Times:144:Times:as  evidence  that  the  skill  content  of  its  exports  is  likely  to  be  much  higher  than  its  
4:95:5751:21:20:90:527:584:144:Times:144:Times:endowment  may  imply.  Schott  (2008)  documents  an  apparent  rapid  increase  in  the  
4:96:5842:20:21:90:524:564:144:Times:144:Times:similarity  between  the  PRC’s  export  structure  and  that  of  high-income  countries,  and 
4:97:5938:21:21:90:525:543:144:Times:144:Times:interprets it as evidence of a rise in the level of sophistication embedded in the country’s 
4:98:6030:21:20:90:529:522:144:Times:144:Times:exports. Wang  and  Wei  (2008a)  use  disaggregated  regional  data  to  investigate  the  
4:99:6122:20:21:90:527:502:144:Times:144:Times:determinants  of  the  rise  in  export  sophistication.  Indeed,  many  other  observers  have  
4:100:6219:21:21:90:529:481:144:Times:144:Times:expressed  fear  that  the  PRC  is  increasingly  producing  and  exporting  sophisticated  
4:101:6312:21:20:90:525:460:144:Times:144:Times:products and may be providing wage competition for mid- to high-skilled workers in the 
4:102:6399:20:21:90:525:440:144:Times:144:Times:US  and  Europe.  However, the  calculations  by  Rodrik  (2006)  and  Schott  (2008)  do  not 
4:103:6494:21:21:90:525:419:144:Times:144:Times:take into account the imported content in the country’s exports. If the domestic content in 
4:104:6586:21:21:90:527:398:144:Times:144:Times:exports from  the  PRC  is  low,  especially  in  sectors  that  would  have  been  considered  
4:105:6682:21:20:90:525:377:144:Times:144:Times:sophisticated  or  high-skilled  in  the  US,  then  imports  from  the  PRC  may  still  generate  a  
4:106:6785:20:21:90:525:357:144:Times:144:Times:large  downward  pressure  on  the  wage  of  the  low-skilled  Americans  after  all  (as  pointed  
4:107:6886:21:21:90:526:336:144:Times:144:Times:out by Krugman, 2008).  These are important policy questions and have implications for 
4:108:6973:21:20:90:525:315:144:Times:144:Times:both developing and developed countries.  A good understanding of the nature and extent 
4:109:7061:20:21:90:525:295:144:Times:144:Times:of global supply chains can provide important insights for economists and policy makers.  
4:110:7151:21:21:126:524:274:144:Times:144:Times:How  would  one  assess  foreign  versus  domestic  content  in  a  country’s  exports? 
4:111:7239:21:20:90:525:253:144:Times:144:Times:Hummels et al. (2001) (HIY in subsequent discussion) propose a method to decompose a 
4:112:7324:20:21:90:525:233:144:Times:144:Times:country’s  exports  into  domestic  and  foreign  value  added share  based  on  a  country’s 
4:113:7418:21:21:90:526:212:144:Times:144:Times:input-output (IO) table.  They  make  a key  assumption  that  the  intensity  in  the  use  of  
4:114:7515:21:21:90:524:191:144:Times:144:Times:imported inputs is the same between production for exports and production for domestic 
4:115:7602:21:20:90:525:170:144:Times:144:Times:sales.  This  assumption  is  violated  in  the  presence  of  processing  exports.  Processing 
4:116:7698:20:21:90:527:150:144:Times:144:Times:exports  are  characterized  by  imports  for  exports  with  favorable  tariff  treatment:  firms  
4:117:7798:21:21:90:525:129:144:Times:144:Times:import parts and other intermediate materials from abroad, with tariff exemptions on the 
4:118:7887:21:20:90:524:108:144:Times:144:Times:imported  inputs  and other tax  preferences  from  local  or  central  governments,  and, after 
4:119:7984:20:0:90:529:88:144:Times:144:Times:processing  or  assembling,  export the  finished  products.  The  policy  preferences  for  
5:120:8079:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:processing  exports  usually  lead  to  a  significant  difference  in  the  intensity  of  imported 
5:121:8179:21:21:90:524:688:144:Times:144:Times:intermediate  inputs  in  the  production  of processing  exports  and  that in  other  demand 
5:122:8274:21:20:90:524:667:144:Times:144:Times:sources  (for  domestic  final  sales  and  normal  exports).    Since  processing  exports  have 
5:123:8372:20:21:89:526:647:144:Times:144:Times:accounted for more than 50% of China's exports every year at least since 1996, the HIY 
5:124:8459:21:21:90:526:626:144:Times:144:Times:formula  is  likely  to  lead  to  a  significant  under-estimation  of  the  share  of  foreign  value  
5:125:8564:21:21:90:527:605:144:Times:144:Times:added  in  its  exports.  In  fact,  most  economies  offer  tariff  reductions  or  exemptions  on  
5:126:8665:21:20:90:525:584:144:Times:144:Times:imported intermediate inputs used in production for exports. Ignoring processing exports 
5:127:8753:20:21:90:526:564:144:Times:144:Times:is  likely  to  lead  to  estimation  errors,  especially  for  economies  that  engage  in  a  massive  
5:128:8858:21:21:90:518:543:144:Times:144:Times:amount of tariff/tax-favored processing trade, such as the China, Mexico and Viet Nam.  
5:129:8946:21:20:126:525:522:144:Times:144:Times:In this paper, we aim to make two contributions to the literature. First, we present 
5:130:9030:20:21:90:525:502:144:Times:144:Times:a  formula  for  computing  shares  of  foreign  and  domestic  value  added  in  a  country’s 
5:131:9125:21:21:90:526:481:144:Times:144:Times:exports  when  processing  exports  are  pervasive.  We  develop  this  formula  because  the  
5:132:9220:21:20:90:528:460:144:Times:144:Times:production  technology  and  input  sourcing  differs  for  goods  produced  for  domestic  
5:133:9312:20:21:90:527:440:144:Times:144:Times:consumption  and  normal  exports  compared  to  those  produced  under  export  processing  
5:134:9405:21:21:90:526:419:144:Times:144:Times:regimes.    The  HIY  formula  is  a  special  case  of  this  general  formula.  Second,  we  apply  
5:135:9507:21:21:90:526:398:144:Times:144:Times:our  methodology  to  China  using  data for  1997,  2002,  and  2007. We  estimate  that  the  
5:136:9603:21:20:90:524:377:144:Times:144:Times:share  of  foreign  value  added  in  China’s  manufactured exports  was  about  50%  during 
5:137:9696:20:21:90:525:357:144:Times:144:Times:1997 to 2002 before China’s WTO membership, almost twice as high as that implied by 
5:138:9780:21:21:90:528:336:144:Times:144:Times:the  HIY  formula,  and  has  risen  to  over  60%  in  2007  after  5  years  of  its  WTO  
5:139:9873:21:20:90:526:315:144:Times:144:Times:membership.  There are also interesting  variations  across  sectors.  Those  sectors  that  are  
5:140:9971:20:21:90:531:295:144:Times:144:Times:likely   labeled   as   relatively   sophisticated   such   as   computers,   telecommunication   
5:141:10069:21:21:90:524:274:144:Times:144:Times:equipments, and electronic devices have particularly low domestic content (about 30% or 
5:142:10157:21:20:90:527:253:144:Times:144:Times:less). By  design,  this  is  an  accounting  exercise,  and  does  not intend  to  examine  the  
5:143:10255:20:21:90:528:233:144:Times:144:Times:determinants,  driving  forces  and  the  consequences  of  changes  in  domestic  contents  in   
5:144:10352:21:21:90:524:212:144:Times:144:Times:China’s gross exports thoroughly. However, a solid methodology to estimate and account 
5:145:10439:21:21:90:524:191:144:Times:144:Times:domestic  and  foreign  value  added  in  developing  countries  exports  is  the  necessary first 
5:146:10538:21:34:90:333:170:144:Times:144:Times:step toward a better understanding of these issues. 
5:147:10590:34:21:126:526:136:144:Times:144:Times:Besides  the  papers  on  vertical  specialization  in  the  international  trade  literature,  
5:148:10686:21:21:90:525:115:144:Times:144:Times:this paper is also related to the I/O literature. In particular, Chen et al. (2004) and Lau et 
5:149:10781:21:0:90:525:94:144:Times:144:Times:al (2007) are the first to develop a “non-competitive”   type I/O model for China (i.e., one 
6:150:10876:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:in which imported and domestically produced inputs are accounted for separately) and to 
6:151:10964:21:21:90:524:688:144:Times:144:Times:incorporate processing  exports  explicitly.  However,  these  papers    do  not  describe  a 
6:152:11058:21:20:90:525:667:144:Times:144:Times:systematic  way  to  infer  separate  input-output  coefficients  for  production  of  processing 
6:153:11156:20:21:90:524:647:144:Times:144:Times:exports versus those for other final demands. It is    therefore difficult for others to replicate 
6:154:11255:21:21:90:525:626:144:Times:144:Times:their  estimates  or  apply  their  methodology  to  other  countries.  In  addition,  they  use  an 
6:155:11356:21:21:90:528:605:144:Times:144:Times:aggregated  version  of  China’s  1995  and  2002  input-output  tables,  respectively,  to  
6:156:11449:21:20:90:522:584:144:Times:144:Times:perform their analysis, with 20 some goods producing industries. We provide a more up-
6:157:11535:20:21:90:527:564:144:Times:144:Times:to-date and more  disaggregated  assessment  of  foreign  and  domestic  values  added  in  
6:158:11627:21:21:90:524:543:144:Times:144:Times:Chinese exports with 83 goods producing industries. Finally, they impose an assumption 
6:159:11714:21:20:90:526:522:144:Times:144:Times:in  estimating  the  import  use  matrix  from  the  competitive  type  I/O  table  published  by  
6:160:11813:20:21:90:527:502:144:Times:144:Times:China’s  National  Statistical  Bureau: within  each  industry,  the  mix  of  the  imported  and  
6:161:11912:21:21:90:530:481:144:Times:144:Times:domestic   inputs   is   the   same   in   capital   formation,   intermediate   inputs,   and   final   
6:162:12017:21:20:90:525:460:144:Times:144:Times:consumption. We  relax  this  assumption  by  refining  a  method  proposed  in  Dean,  Fung, 
6:163:12110:20:21:90:525:440:144:Times:144:Times:and  Wang  (2007)  that  combines  China’s  processing  imports  statistics  with  United 
6:164:12200:21:35:90:392:419:144:Times:144:Times:Nations Broad Economic Categories (UNBEC) classification.  
6:165:12259:35:21:126:524:384:144:Times:144:Times:The  rest  of  the  paper  is  organized  as  follows.  Section  2 presents  a conceptual 
6:166:12349:21:20:90:525:363:144:Times:144:Times:framework  for estimating  shares  of  domestic  and  foreign  value  added  in  a  country’s 
6:167:12443:20:21:90:531:343:144:Times:144:Times:exports   when   processing   exports   are   pervasive.   It   also   describes   a   mathematic   
6:168:12543:21:21:90:526:322:144:Times:144:Times:programming procedure to systematically infer a set of I/O coefficients called for by the 
6:169:12633:21:20:90:524:301:144:Times:144:Times:new formula but not typically available from a conventional I/O table. Section 3 presents 
6:170:12723:20:21:90:528:281:144:Times:144:Times:the  estimation  results  for  Chinese  exports.  Section  4  evaluate  the  accuracy  of  the  
6:171:12819:21:21:90:526:260:144:Times:144:Times:estimation  results  by  using  an  IO  table  with  separate  processing  trade  account  complied  
6:172:12920:21:20:90:524:239:144:Times:144:Times:by Mexico national statistical agency based 2003 economic census.  Section 5 concludes.  
6:173:13009:20:21:90:93:219:144:Times:144:Times: 
6:174:13009:21:21:90:351:198:144:Times:144:Times:2. Conceptual Framework and Estimation Method 
6:175:13054:21:21:90:471:177:144:Times:144:Times:2.1 When special features of processing exports are not taken into account 
6:176:13128:21:20:90:93:156:144:Times:144:Times: 
6:177:13128:20:21:126:525:136:144:Times:144:Times:We first discuss how domestic and foreign contents in a country’s exports can be 
6:178:13209:21:21:90:526:115:144:Times:144:Times:computed  when  it  does  not  engage  in  any  processing  trade.  The  discussion  follows  the  
6:179:13308:21:0:90:525:94:144:Times:144:Times:input-output literature, and is the approach adopted (implicitly) by Hummels et al. (2001) 
7:180:13401:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:and Yi (2003). Along the way, we will point out a clear connection between the domestic 
7:181:13489:21:21:90:375:688:144:Times:65:Times:content concept and the concept of vertical specialization. 2
7:182:13550:21:20:126:525:667:144:Times:144:Times:When  imported  and  domestically  produced  intermediate inputs  are  accounted 
7:183:13631:20:0:90:434:647:144:Times:144:Times:separately, a value-based input-output table can be specified as follows:
7:184:13704:0:36:375:378:688:144:Times:144:Times:

7:188:13705:23:23:196:503:624:143:Times:144:Times:XYXADD=+        (1) 
7:189:13717:23:22:196:503:601:143:Times:144:Times:MYXAMM=+        (2) 
7:190:13729:22:24:215:503:579:142:Times:144:Times:uAuAuAvMD=++          (3) 
7:191:13749:24:21:90:524:555:144:Times:144:Times:where AD = [aDij] is an xnn matrix of direct input coefficients of domestic products; AM = 
7:192:13837:21:21:90:526:534:144:Times:144:Times:[aMij] is  an  xnn  matrix  of  direct inputs  of  imported  goods; YD is  an  1xn  vector  of  final  
7:193:13937:21:21:89:525:513:144:Times:144:Times:demands for domestically produced products, including usage in gross capital formation, 
7:194:14025:21:20:89:525:492:144:Times:144:Times:private  and  public  final consumption,  and  gross  exports; YM  is  an n×1  vector  of  final 
7:195:14120:20:21:90:526:472:144:Times:144:Times:demands for imported products, including usages in gross capital formation, private  and  
7:196:14210:21:21:90:524:451:144:Times:144:Times:public final consumption; X is a n×1 vector of gross output; M is a n×1 vector of imports; 
7:197:14301:21:21:90:531:430:144:Times:144:Times:Av = [avj]  is a 1×n vector of each sector j’s ratio of value added to gross output, and u   is a 
7:198:14398:21:20:90:524:409:144:Times:144:Times:1×n  unity vector. Subscripts i and j indicate sectors, and superscripts D and M represent 
7:199:14488:20:21:90:382:389:144:Times:144:Times:domestically produced and imported products, respectively.  
7:200:14548:21:21:126:526:368:144:Times:144:Times:Equations  (1)  and  (2)  define  two  horizontal  balance  conditions  for  domestically  
7:201:14639:21:20:90:526:347:144:Times:144:Times:produced  and  imported  products,  respectively.  A  typical  row  k  in  Equation  (1)  specifies  
7:202:14740:20:21:89:526:327:144:Times:144:Times:that  total  domestic  production  of  product  k  should  be  equal  to  the  sum  of  the  sales  of  
7:203:14844:21:21:89:530:306:144:Times:144:Times:product k  to  all  intermediate  and  final  users  in  the  economy  (  the  final  sales  include 
7:204:14945:21:20:89:524:285:144:Times:144:Times:domestic consumption and capital formation, plus exports of product k).    A typical row h 
7:205:15035:20:21:89:525:265:144:Times:144:Times:in Equation (2) specifies that the total imports of product h should be equal to the sum of 
7:206:15126:21:21:89:526:244:144:Times:144:Times:the  sales  of  product  h  to  all  users in  the  economy,  including  intermediate  inputs  for  all  
7:207:15231:21:21:89:524:223:144:Times:144:Times:sectors,  plus  final  domestic  consumption  and  capital  formation.  Equation  (3) is both  a 
7:208:15328:21:24:89:528:202:144:Times:144:Times:vertical  balance  condition,  and  an  adding-up constraint  for  the  input-output  coefficients.  
7:209:15429:24:7:234:237:178:144:Times:144:Times:                                                 
7:210:15477:7:16:90:521:171:42:Times:99:Times:2 We use the terms “domestic value added”   and “domestic content”   interchangeably. Similarly, we use the 
7:211:15585:16:12:90:498:155:99:Times:99:Times:terms “foreign value added”, “ foreign content”, and “ vertical specialization”   to mean the same thing.  
7:212:15691:12:7:90:92:143:99:Times:99:Times: 
7:213:15691:7:16:90:524:136:42:Times:99:Times:3  Such  a  model  is  called  a  “non-competitive”   model  in  the  IO  literature.  HIY  (2001)  do  not  specify this 
7:214:15813:16:12:89:529:120:99:Times:99:Times:system explicitly but  go  straight  to  the  implied  Leontief  inverse  while Chen et al. (2004) specify   only  the

7:216:16051:11:11:89:525:97:99:Times:99:Times:vertical specialization and domestic content, and a comparison with the model in the next sub-section that 
7:217:16158:11:12:89:203:86:99:Times:99:Times:features processing exports.

9:256:18268:0:20:90:448:708:144:Times:144:Times:2.2 Domestic Content in Exports When Processing Trade is Prevalent 
9:257:18334:20:21:126:524:688:144:Times:144:Times:We now turn to the case in which tariff-favored processing exports are prevalent; 
9:258:18416:21:20:90:526:667:144:Times:144:Times:these  exports  have a  different  intensity  in  the  use  of  imported  inputs  than  do  domestic  
9:259:18518:20:21:90:525:647:144:Times:144:Times:final sales (and normal exports). Conceptually, we wish to keep track separately of the IO 
9:260:18608:21:21:90:528:626:144:Times:144:Times:coefficients  of  the  processing  exports  and  those  of  domestic  final  sales  and  normal  
9:261:18705:21:21:89:528:605:144:Times:144:Times:exports.  For  now,  we  ignore  the  fact  that  these IO  coefficients  may  not  be  directly  
9:262:18803:21:20:90:502:584:144:Times:144:Times:available, and will discuss a formal approach to estimate them in the next subsection.

11:605:22512:37:24:90:525:283:144:Times:144:Times:Either when DDA = DPA and DvA =PvA, or when EP/te = 0, Equation (20) reduces to the 
11:606:22596:24:21:90:527:259:144:Times:144:Times:HIY  formula  in  Equation  (5).  Note  we  can  easily  verify  that  for  both  processing  and  
11:607:22695:21:21:90:448:238:144:Times:144:Times:normal exports, the sum of domestic and foreign content shares is unity.    
11:608:22771:21:20:90:93:217:144:Times:144:Times: 
11:609:22771:20:21:90:200:197:144:Times:144:Times:2.3 Estimation Issues 
11:610:22792:21:20:126:525:176:144:Times:144:Times: Equations  (18-20)  allows  us  to  compute  the shares of  domestic  content  in 
11:611:22873:20:21:90:525:156:144:Times:144:Times:processing  and  normal  exports for  each  industry  as  well  as  in  a  country’s  total  exports. 
11:612:22975:21:21:90:524:135:144:Times:144:Times:However, statistical  agencies  typically  only  report  a traditional I/O  matrix, AD,  and 
11:613:23068:21:21:90:524:114:144:Times:144:Times:sometimes AM, but not ADP, ADD, AMP and AMD separately. Therefore, a method to estimate 
11:614:23155:21:0:90:525:93:144:Times:144:Times:these  matrices,  based  on  available  information,  has  to  be  developed. In  this  sub-section, 
12:615:23259:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:we  propose  to  do  this  via  a  quadratic  programming  model  by  combining information 
12:616:23351:21:21:90:328:688:144:Times:144:Times:from trade statistics and conventional I/O tables.  
12:617:23402:21:20:125:525:667:144:Times:144:Times: The basic idea of this model is to use information from the standard  I/O table to 
12:618:23485:20:21:89:527:647:144:Times:144:Times:determine  sector-level  total  imports/exports,  and  information  from  trade  statistics  to  
12:619:23582:21:21:89:524:626:144:Times:144:Times:determine  the  relative  proportion  of  processing  and  normal  exports  within  each  sector, 
12:620:23680:21:21:89:521:605:144:Times:144:Times:thus  use  up  all  available  data  to  split  the  national  economy  into  processing  and  non-
12:621:23779:21:20:89:526:584:144:Times:144:Times:processing  blocks,  each  with  its  own  IO  structure.  Using  the  data  from  the  I/O  table  to  
12:622:23883:20:21:89:525:564:144:Times:144:Times:determine sector-level total imports/exports helps to ensure that the balance conditions in 
12:623:23975:21:21:89:528:543:144:Times:144:Times:the  official  I/O  account  are  always  satisfied,  and  that  the  I/O  table  with  separate  
12:624:24073:21:20:89:527:522:144:Times:144:Times:processing  and  non-processing accounts  estimated  from  the  model  always  sums  to  the  
12:625:24167:20:21:89:526:502:144:Times:144:Times:published  official  table.  Such  a  method  is  a  formalization  of  the  calibration  methods  
12:626:24266:21:21:89:527:481:144:Times:144:Times:widely  used  in  macroeconomics and  CGE  modeling  when  the  number  of  endogenous  
12:627:24354:21:20:89:315:460:144:Times:144:Times:variables larger than the number of equations.  
12:628:24402:20:23:125:422:440:144:Times:144:Times: The following data are observable from a standard I/O table:  
12:629:24464:23:19:134:272:417:144:Times:144:Times: ix= Gross output of sector i;  
12:630:24495:19:21:133:380:398:144:Times:144:Times: ijz= Goods i used as intermediate inputs in sector j;  
12:631:24550:21:19:134:269:377:144:Times:144:Times: jv= Value-added in sector j;  
12:632:24579:19:19:136:333:358:144:Times:144:Times: im = Total imports of sector i goods; and  
12:633:24622:19:24:134:384:339:144:Times:144:Times: iy=Total final demand except for exports of goods i. 
12:634:24675:24:43:90:521:315:144:Times:65:Times: ` We combine those observed data from the I/O table and processing trade shares5
12:635:24756:43:0:126:129:272:144:Times:144:Times:  
12:636:24756:0:21:522:525:315:144:Times:144:Times: 
12:637:24756:21:17:90:368:294:144:Times:144:Times:observed from trade statistics to determine the values for: 
12:638:24816:17:8:141:145:277:48:Times:48:Times:p
12:639:24817:8:14:139:525:269:48:Times:144:Times:im = Imports of sector i good used as intermediate inputs to produce processing 
12:640:24897:14:16:90:134:255:144:Times:144:Times:exports;  
12:641:24907:16:16:137:529:239:144:Times:144:Times: dim  =  Imports  of  sector  i  goods  used  as  intermediate  inputs  for  domestic  
12:642:24993:16:16:90:247:223:144:Times:144:Times:production and normal exports;  
12:643:25025:16:19:134:305:207:144:Times:144:Times: nie= Normal exports of sector i ; and 
12:644:25062:19:24:134:306:188:144:Times:144:Times: pie = Processing exports of sector i.   
12:645:25101:24:20:126:525:164:144:Times:144:Times: The partition of imports into intermediate and final use is based on a combination 
12:646:25184:20:24:90:525:144:144:Times:144:Times:of China custom import statistics and UN BEC classification, as described in Dean, Fang 
12:647:25272:24:7:234:237:120:144:Times:144:Times:                                                 
12:648:25320:7:16:90:519:113:42:Times:99:Times:5 Processing trade are defined by China Customs, which include trade regime “Process & assembling "(14) 
12:649:25423:16:11:90:497:97:99:Times:99:Times:and “Process with imported materials" (15) in China Customs statistics. These statistics are relatively 
12:650:25527:11:12:90:519:86:99:Times:99:Times:accurate because they involve duty exemption and value-added tax rebates which under intensive Customs 
12:651:25630:12:0:90:141:74:99:Times:99:Times:monitoring.  
13:652:25645:0:21:90:527:709:144:Times:144:Times:and  Wang  (2011). The  results  of  such  partition  and  the  actual  numbers  used  in  our  
13:653:25741:21:21:90:525:688:144:Times:144:Times:empirical  estimation  are  reported  and  discussed  in  the  data  source  subsection  later. 
13:654:25837:21:20:90:524:667:144:Times:144:Times:Parameters on  domestic  and  imported  final  demand  can  be  inferred  from  the  observed 
13:655:25931:20:23:90:202:647:144:Times:144:Times:data discussed above:   
13:656:25954:23:19:135:485:624:144:Times:144:Times: miy= Final demand of goods i from imports (residuals of im- pim - dim);  
13:657:26027:19:20:135:525:605:144:Times:144:Times: diy=  Final  demand  of  goods  i  provided  by  domestic  production  (residual  of  iy- 
13:658:26117:20:9:99:104:585:49:Times:49:Times:m
13:659:26118:9:20:98:120:576:49:Times:144:Times:iy).  
13:660:26124:20:23:90:511:556:144:Times:144:Times:All those data based on official statistics are entered our estimation model as constants. 
13:661:26214:23:28:126:525:533:144:Times:144:Times:Define ddijz=  Domestically  produced  intermediate  good  i  used  by  sector  j  for 
13:662:26300:28:27:89:525:505:144:Times:144:Times:domestic  sales  and  normal  exports; dpijz=  Domestically  produced  intermediate  good  i

13:666:26617:0:9:261:265:435:50:Times:50:Times:d

14:823:27629:24:21:125:527:406:144:Times:144:Times:The  economic  meanings  of  these  9  groups  of  constraints  are  straightforward.  
14:824:27716:21:20:89:525:385:144:Times:144:Times:Equations (21) and (22) are row sum identities for the expanded I/O account. They state 
14:825:27804:20:21:89:524:365:144:Times:144:Times:that total gross output of sector i has to equal to the sum of domestic intermediaries, final 
14:826:27898:21:21:89:525:344:144:Times:144:Times:demand and exports (both processing and normal exports) in that sector. Similarly, total 
14:827:27987:21:20:89:528:323:144:Times:144:Times:imports have to equal imported intermediate inputs plus imports delivered to final users.  
14:828:28078:20:21:89:526:303:144:Times:144:Times:Equations  (23)  and  (24)  are  column  sum  identities  for  the  expanded  I/O  account.  They  
14:829:28177:21:21:89:526:282:144:Times:144:Times:define  the  value  of  processing  exports  in  sector  j  as  the  sum  of  domestic  and  imported  
14:830:28280:21:21:89:524:261:144:Times:144:Times:intermediate inputs as well as primary factors used in producing processing exports; t hese 
14:831:28371:21:20:89:526:240:144:Times:144:Times:four  groups  of  constraints  correspond  to equations  (7)-(10)  in  the  extended  I/O  model  
14:832:28469:20:21:89:525:220:144:Times:144:Times:respectively.  Equations  (25)  to  (29)  are  a  set  of  adding  up  constraints  to  ensure  that  the  
14:833:28576:21:21:89:527:199:144:Times:144:Times:solution  from  the  model  is  consistent  with  official  statistics  on  sector-level  trade  and  
14:834:28678:21:20:89:526:178:144:Times:144:Times:within-industry  transactions. Suppose  there  are  K  sectors,  then  there  will  be  4K2  +  2K  
14:835:28778:20:21:89:525:158:144:Times:144:Times:unknowns  and  only  7K+K2 independent  constraints,  so  we  have  to  cast  the  calibration 
14:836:28872:21:21:90:524:137:144:Times:144:Times:problem  as  a  constrained  optimization  procedure  to  minimize  following  objective 
14:837:28961:21:0:90:141:116:144:Times:144:Times:functions:

15:1017:30650:34:23:126:525:123:144:Times:144:Times:The initial values for direct value  added in the production for processing exports 
15:1018:30734:23:25:90:525:100:144:Times:144:Times:in  sector  j  (pjv0  ), are generally  set  to  be  the  residuals  implied  by  Equation  (24). 
15:1019:30832:25:0:89:525:75:144:Times:144:Times:However, we set a minimum value at the sum of labor compensation and depreciation in 
16:1020:30920:0:23:90:524:709:144:Times:144:Times:a sector multiplied by the share of processing exports in that sector’s total output. In other 
16:1021:31015:23:25:90:524:686:144:Times:144:Times:words, the initial value pjv0 is set to equal the greater of the residuals from Equation (24) 
16:1022:31109:25:23:90:527:661:144:Times:144:Times:or  the  minimum  value.  The  initial  value  for  direct  value  added  in  the  production  for  
16:1023:31209:23:28:90:525:638:144:Times:144:Times:domestic sales and normal exports (djv0) is set as the difference between jv (from the I/O 
16:1024:31300:28:24:90:170:610:144:Times:144:Times:table) and pjv0.  
16:1025:31317:24:21:125:525:586:144:Times:144:Times:We conduct some sensitivity checks using alternative initial values to empirically 
16:1026:31400:21:21:89:526:565:144:Times:144:Times:verify  whether  the  model  solutions  are  sensitive  to  these  initial  values.  It  turns  out  that  
16:1027:31507:21:20:89:529:544:144:Times:144:Times:these   alternative   initial   values   do   not   materially   alter   our   basic   conclusions.   We   
16:1028:31614:20:21:89:525:524:144:Times:144:Times:implement  this  quadratic  programming  model  in  GAMS  (Brooke et  al,  2005),  related 
16:1029:31705:21:21:89:530:503:144:Times:144:Times:computer programs   and   data   files   will   be   available   at   the   USITC   website   for   
16:1030:31805:21:20:89:167:482:144:Times:144:Times:downloading.    
16:1031:31821:20:21:125:128:462:144:Times:144:Times: 
16:1032:31821:21:26:89:204:441:144:Times:144:Times:3. Estimation Results  
16:1033:31842:26:21:125:525:415:144:Times:144:Times: After describing the data sources, we report and discuss the estimation results for 
16:1034:31926:21:20:89:525:394:144:Times:144:Times:shares of domestic and foreign content in Chinese exports at the aggregate level, and by 
16:1035:32015:20:21:89:358:374:144:Times:144:Times:sector, firm ownership and major destination countries. 
16:1036:32071:21:21:90:165:353:144:Times:144:Times:3.1 Data  
16:1037:32079:21:20:108:526:332:144:Times:144:Times:Inter-industry transaction and (direct) value-added data are from China’s 1997, 2002 
16:1038:32164:20:21:89:525:312:144:Times:144:Times:and  2007  benchmark  I/O  tables  published  by  the National  Bureau  of  Statistics  of  China  
16:1039:32263:21:21:89:527:291:144:Times:144:Times:(NBS).  We  use  detailed  exports  and  imports  data  of 1997,  2002,  and  2007  from  the  
16:1040:32358:21:21:89:525:270:144:Times:144:Times:General Customs Administration of China to help differentiate the processing and normal 
16:1041:32446:21:20:89:524:249:144:Times:144:Times:trade in each sector.  The trade statistics are first aggregated from the 8-digit HS level to 
16:1042:32540:20:21:90:524:229:144:Times:144:Times:China’s I/O industries, and then used to compute the share of processing exports in each 
16:1043:32629:21:21:90:525:208:144:Times:144:Times:I/O  industry. Modifying  a  method  from  Dean,  Fung  and  Wang  (2009),  we  partition  all 
16:1044:32724:21:20:90:527:187:144:Times:144:Times:imports in  a  given  commodity  classification  into  three  parts  based  on  the  distinction  
16:1045:32822:20:21:89:528:167:144:Times:144:Times:between  processing  and  normal  imports  in  the trade  statistics,  and on the  UN  BEC  
16:1046:32914:21:21:89:525:146:144:Times:144:Times:classification  scheme:    (a) intermediate  inputs in  producing  processing  exports;  (b) 
16:1047:33007:21:20:89:527:125:144:Times:144:Times:intermediate inputs for normal exports and other domestic final sales;  and (c) those used 
16:1048:33098:20:21:89:524:105:144:Times:144:Times:in gross capital formation and final consumption. A summary of these trade statistics as a 
16:1049:33189:21:0:89:522:84:144:Times:144:Times:percentage of China’s total imports along with share of processing exports during 1996-
17:1050:33279:0:21:90:527:709:144:Times:144:Times:2008  is  reported  in Table 1,  which shows  a  downward  trend  for  the  use  of  imported  
17:1051:33374:21:21:89:526:688:144:Times:144:Times:inputs  in  producing  processing  exports,  and  an  upward  trend  in  their  use  in  producing  
17:1052:33474:21:20:90:527:667:144:Times:144:Times:normal  trade  and  domestic  final  sales.  Processing  exports  as  a  share  of  China’s  total  
17:1053:33574:20:21:90:527:647:144:Times:144:Times:merchandise  exports  also  gradually  decline  in  recent  years.  Such  trend  seems  partially  
17:1054:33673:21:21:90:527:626:144:Times:144:Times:reflects  the  consequence  of  a  series  of  policy  measures  to  change  the  preferences  to  
17:1055:33772:21:21:90:524:605:144:Times:144:Times:processing  trade  and  foreign  invested  enterprises  has  adopted  by  Chinese  government 
17:1056:33866:21:20:89:201:584:144:Times:144:Times:since the end of 2006.

17:1064:34293:20:21:90:348:419:144:Times:99:Times:3.2 Domestic and foreign contents in total exports  
17:1065:34344:21:21:126:528:398:144:Times:144:Times: Table 2 presents  the results  for  the  decomposition  of aggregate foreign  and  
17:1066:34427:21:20:90:524:377:144:Times:144:Times:domestic value-added shares in 1997, 2002 and 2007.  For comparison, the results from 
17:1067:34513:20:21:89:524:357:144:Times:144:Times:the HIY method that ignores   processing trade are also reported.  The estimated aggregate 
17:1068:34604:21:21:90:525:336:144:Times:144:Times:domestic value added share in China’s merchandise exports was 54% in 1997, and 60.6% 
17:1069:34689:21:20:90:525:315:144:Times:144:Times:in  2007.  For  manufacturing  products,  these  estimated  shares  are  slightly  lower  in  levels 
17:1070:34790:20:21:89:525:295:144:Times:144:Times:but  trending  upward  significantly at  50%  in  1997  and  59.7%  in  2007,  respectively.  In 
17:1071:34887:21:21:89:526:274:144:Times:144:Times:general,  the estimated  direct  domestic  value-added  shares  are  less  than  half  of  the  total  
17:1072:34990:21:20:89:526:253:144:Times:144:Times:domestic value-added shares. However, the estimated indirect foreign value-added share 
17:1073:35077:20:21:89:525:233:144:Times:144:Times:was  relatively  small;  most  of  the  foreign  content  comes  from  directly  imported  foreign  
17:1074:35177:21:21:89:525:212:144:Times:144:Times:inputs, especially in 1997 and 2002. The indirect foreign value-added increase over time, 
17:1075:35267:21:21:89:525:191:144:Times:144:Times:and reach about a quarter of China’s directly imported foreign inputs in 2007, indicating 
17:1076:35357:21:20:89:525:170:144:Times:144:Times:the  share  of  simple  processing  and  assembling  of  foreign  parts  is  declining,  while  more  
17:1077:35459:20:21:89:525:150:144:Times:144:Times:imported intermediates are being used in the production of other intermediate inputs that 
17:1078:35549:21:21:89:291:129:144:Times:144:Times:are then used in the production process.    
17:1079:35593:21:0:125:230:108:144:Times:144:Times: (Insert table 2 here) 
18:1080:35617:0:21:126:524:709:144:Times:144:Times:Relative to the estimates from the HIY method, our procedure produces estimates 
18:1081:35697:21:21:90:525:688:144:Times:144:Times:of a  much  higher  share  of  foreign  value  added  in  Chinese  gross  exports  and  with  a 
18:1082:35793:21:20:90:526:667:144:Times:144:Times:different trend over time. To be more precise, estimates from the HIY method show that 
18:1083:35880:20:21:90:527:647:144:Times:144:Times:the  foreign  content  share  (total  VS  share)  increased  steadily from  17.6%  in  1997  to  
18:1084:35977:21:21:90:525:626:144:Times:144:Times:28.7% in 2007 for all merchandise exports, and from 19.0% to 27.1% for manufacturing 
18:1085:36062:21:21:90:527:605:144:Times:144:Times:only  during  the  same  period.  In  contrast,  our  estimates  suggest  a  trend  in  the  opposite  
18:1086:36165:21:20:90:525:584:144:Times:144:Times:direction, with  the  share  of  foreign  value  added  in  all  merchandise  exports  falling  from  
18:1087:36267:20:21:90:525:564:144:Times:144:Times:46%  in  1997  to  39.4%  in  2007,  and  a  similar  decline for  the  share  in  manufacturing 
18:1088:36364:21:21:89:526:543:144:Times:144:Times:exports,  it  fell  from  50%  in  1997  to  40.3%  in  2007.  The  decline  occur  mainly  during  
18:1089:36464:21:20:89:524:522:144:Times:144:Times:2002-2007  period,  which  corresponds  to  the  first  5  years  of  China’s  entry  to  the  WTO. 
18:1090:36564:20:21:89:525:502:144:Times:144:Times:Our estimates indicate that the HIY method appears to incorrectly estimate both the level 
18:1091:36654:21:21:90:430:481:144:Times:144:Times:and the trend in domestic versus foreign content in the PRC’s exports. 
18:1092:36725:21:20:126:525:460:144:Times:144:Times:What accounts for the difference between ours and HIY approaches? There are at 
18:1093:36804:20:21:90:526:440:144:Times:144:Times:least three factors drive the change of foreign content of the country’s gross exports: (1) 
18:1094:36896:21:21:90:527:419:144:Times:144:Times:the  relative  proportions  of  its  total  imports  used  as  intermediate  inputs   in  producing  
18:1095:36997:21:21:90:527:398:144:Times:144:Times:processing  exports  and  domestic  sales  &  normal  exports;  (2)  the  share  of  processing  
18:1096:37094:21:20:90:524:377:144:Times:144:Times:exports in  its  total  exports;  and  (3)  the  sector  composition  of  its  exports.  Because 
18:1097:37191:20:21:90:525:357:144:Times:144:Times:processing exports tend to use substantially more imported inputs, and processing exports 
18:1098:37281:21:21:90:528:336:144:Times:144:Times:account  for  a  major  share  of  China’s  total  exports, the  HIY  indicator is likely  to  
18:1099:37376:21:20:90:526:315:144:Times:144:Times:substantially underestimate the true for foreign content in China’s exports. This explains 
18:1100:37467:20:21:90:528:295:144:Times:144:Times:the  level  of  domestic  content  by  our  measure  is  much  lower  than  that  of  the  HIY  
18:1101:37563:21:21:90:525:274:144:Times:144:Times:indicator. On the other hand, as exporting firms (both those producing for normal exports 
18:1102:37653:21:20:90:527:253:144:Times:144:Times:and  those  for  processing  exports)  gradually  increase  their  intermediate  inputs  sourcing  
18:1103:37752:20:21:90:527:233:144:Times:144:Times:from  firms  within  China  or  multinationals  move  their  upstream  production  to  be  near  
18:1104:37849:21:21:90:526:212:144:Times:144:Times:their  downstream  production,  the  extent  of  domestic  content  in  exports  rose  over  time.  
18:1105:37949:21:21:90:527:191:144:Times:144:Times:This  exactly  is  what  has  happened  since  China  joining  the  WTO.  However,  because  
18:1106:38042:21:20:90:526:170:144:Times:144:Times:exports  from  industries  with  relatively  lower  domestic  content  often  grow  faster  due  to  
18:1107:38143:20:21:90:525:150:144:Times:144:Times:dramatic inflow of foreign direct investment, the composition of  a countries total exports 
18:1108:38235:21:21:90:527:129:144:Times:144:Times:may  play  as  an  offsetting  factor  to  reduce  the  share  of  domestic  value-added  in  the  
18:1109:38334:21:20:90:525:108:144:Times:144:Times:country’s  gross  exports  thus  slow  down  the  increase  of  domestic  value-added  share  in  a  
18:1110:38435:20:0:90:525:88:144:Times:144:Times:country’s  total  exports.  As  Chinese  government  start  to reduce  the  policy  incentives  for  
19:1111:38539:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:both Foreign Invested Enterprises (FIE) and processing exports at the end of 2006, we are 
19:1112:38629:21:21:90:526:688:144:Times:144:Times:observing  a  trend  of  increasing  domestic  contents  in  Chinese  exports  as  China  continue  
19:1113:38729:21:20:90:307:667:144:Times:144:Times:its industrial upgrading in the years to come. 
19:1114:38776:20:21:126:525:647:144:Times:144:Times:Our interpretation is confirmed by DVA shares for processing and normal exports 
19:1115:38856:21:21:90:525:626:144:Times:144:Times:estimated separately (Table 3). There is a more than 10 percentage point increase in the 
19:1116:38945:21:21:90:525:605:144:Times:144:Times:total foreign value-added share for domestic sales and normal exports between 1997 and 
19:1117:39032:21:20:90:529:584:144:Times:144:Times:2007,  which  is  consistent  with  the  trend  indicated  by  HIY  measure.  However,  in  
19:1118:39124:20:21:90:528:564:144:Times:144:Times:processing  exports  we  see  that  more  domestic-produced  inputs  were  used,  domestic  
19:1119:39216:21:21:90:526:543:144:Times:144:Times:value-added  share  increased  from  20.7%  in  1997  to  37.0%  in  2007,  up  more  than  16  
19:1120:39312:21:20:90:526:522:144:Times:144:Times:percentage  point.  Because  processing  exports  still  constitute  more  than  50%  of  China’s  
19:1121:39411:20:21:90:525:502:144:Times:144:Times:total  exports  in  2007,  which  resulting  the  weighted  average  total  domestic  value-added 
19:1122:39509:21:21:90:262:481:144:Times:144:Times:share went up during the decades.   
19:1123:39545:21:20:126:525:460:144:Times:144:Times:There are conflicting forces at work. On the one hand, as domestic input suppliers 
19:1124:39628:20:21:90:529:440:144:Times:144:Times:increase  their  quality  over  time,  and  multinationals  move  more  and  more  of  their  
19:1125:39722:21:21:90:525:419:144:Times:144:Times:upstream production into China, exporting firms may decide to increase local sourcing of 
19:1126:39811:21:21:90:528:398:144:Times:144:Times:their  inputs.  On  the  other  hand,  the  reductions  in  the  country’s  trade  barriers  also  
19:1127:39910:21:20:90:528:377:144:Times:144:Times:encourage  exporting  firms  to  use  more  imported  inputs.  These  two  opposing  forces  
19:1128:40003:20:21:90:528:357:144:Times:144:Times:partially  offset  each  other.  However,  on  net,  the  domestic  content  share  in  China’s  
19:1129:40100:21:21:90:528:336:144:Times:144:Times:exports  appears  to  be  on  the  rise.    Looking  ahead,  the  share  of  imported  content  in  
19:1130:40200:21:20:90:527:315:144:Times:144:Times:exports  could  fall  or  rise,  depending  on  the  relative  speed  with  which  domestic  input  
19:1131:40300:20:21:90:526:295:144:Times:144:Times:suppliers  and  multi-nationals  can  step  up  their  quality  and  variety  versus  the  extent  of  
19:1132:40403:21:21:90:370:274:144:Times:144:Times:additional reductions in the cost of using imported inputs. 
19:1133:40463:21:19:90:193:253:144:Times:144:Times:(insert table 3 here)

19:1136:40564:21:23:90:525:200:144:Times:144:Times:to alternative ways of setting the initial values of the variables and the share parameters 
19:1137:40656:23:24:89:525:177:144:Times:144:Times:of import use. First, we initialize pjv0 and djv0 by apportioning the observed direct value 
19:1138:40748:24:24:90:525:153:144:Times:144:Times:added in a sector to processing exports and other final demands based on their respective

19:1140:40937:24:21:90:528:105:144:Times:144:Times:implied  by  equation  (24)  if  the  residuals  are  positive,  or  by  following  the  previous  
19:1141:41036:21:0:90:528:84:144:Times:144:Times:alternative  if  the  residuals  are  non-positive.  Third,  when  we  partition  imports  into  
20:1142:41136:0:21:90:529:709:144:Times:144:Times:different  users,  we  use  the  average  of  a  three-year  period  (previous,  current,  and  
20:1143:41232:21:21:89:527:688:144:Times:144:Times:following  years)  rather  than  just  one  year’s  statistics.  Fourth,  we  experiment  with  0%  
20:1144:41332:21:20:89:529:667:144:Times:144:Times:versus   10%   annual   depreciation   rate   for   capital   goods.   These   variations   produce   
20:1145:41434:20:21:89:525:647:144:Times:144:Times:relatively little change in the main results. For example, the estimated share of domestic 
20:1146:41524:21:21:90:526:626:144:Times:144:Times:value  added  in  manufacturing  exports  lies  in  a  relatively  narrow  range  between  ?%  and  
20:1147:41624:21:21:89:313:605:144:Times:144:Times:?% in 2002, and between ?% and ?% in 2007.

20:1149:41666:20:21:90:354:564:144:Times:144:Times:3.3 Domestic content in exports by firm ownership  
20:1150:41717:21:21:126:525:543:144:Times:144:Times:Since  foreign-invested  firms  account  for  over  half  of  China’s  exports,  compare

20:1158:42410:21:20:126:525:377:144:Times:144:Times:Estimates of the domestic content shares by firm ownership are presented in Table

20:1167:43223:21:21:126:525:191:144:Times:144:Times: The most noticeable feature of this table is the raising domestic contents in export 
20:1168:43308:21:20:90:526:170:144:Times:144:Times:produced by foreign invested firms, their DVA share increased more than 10 percentage 
20:1169:43394:20:21:90:528:150:144:Times:144:Times:points  between  2002  to  2007(There  is  a  10.5%  percentage  point  increase  for  wholly  
20:1170:43489:21:21:90:527:129:144:Times:144:Times:Foreign  Owned  firms,  and  a  13.6  percentage  point  increase  for  joint  ventures),  while  
20:1171:43587:21:20:90:525:108:144:Times:144:Times:DVA share of Chinese domestic firms basically stay steady during the same period. This

21:1173:43780:0:21:90:526:709:144:Times:144:Times:China  in  WTO  is  mainly  due  to  FIE  sourcing  more  of  their  intermediate  inputs  within  
21:1174:43879:21:21:90:527:688:144:Times:144:Times:China.  This  is  consistent  with  the  observation  of  more  and  more  multinationals  move  
21:1175:43976:21:20:90:525:667:144:Times:144:Times:their upstream production to China getting closer to their downstream production already 
21:1176:44065:20:21:90:480:647:144:Times:144:Times:in China and FIE using more and more intermediate inputs from local suppliers.  
21:1177:44145:21:21:126:527:626:144:Times:144:Times: Further  exam  the  change  of  domestic  value-added  share  across  firms  with  the

21:1183:44698:20:21:90:526:502:144:Times:144:Times:processing  exports  using  more  locally  supplied  intermediate  inputs  in  2007  than  that  in  
21:1184:44799:21:41:90:118:481:144:Times:65:Times:20026

21:1194:45309:21:20:90:522:308:144:Times:144:Times:structure, Tables 5 and 6 report, in ascending order on domestic content share, the value-

22:1207:46487:0:21:90:526:709:144:Times:144:Times:nearly  35  percent  of  China’s  merchandise  exports  that  year.  Many  low-DVA  industries

24:1279:52301:20:20:90:320:564:144:Times:144:Times:4. The accuracy of Content Share Estimates  
24:1280:52344:20:19:126:524:544:122:Times:122:Times: As   we   discussed   earlier,   the   estimation   procedure   presented   in   this   paper   is   a 
24:1281:52447:19:19:90:526:525:122:Times:122:Times:formalization and  extension  of calibration  methods  widely  used in  macroeconomics  and  CGE  
24:1282:52545:19:20:89:524:506:122:Times:122:Times:modeling. Different  from  econometric  model,  evaluation  on  the  accuracy  of  the  calibration 
24:1283:52644:20:21:89:525:486:122:Times:144:Times:largely  rely  on a benchmark data set from the real world. However, it is not  very  easy  to  find 
24:1284:52745:21:20:90:534:465:144:Times:144:Times:such  a  benchmark  data  set  to  assess the  accuracy  of  results  from  our  estimation  method      
24:1285:52850:20:21:90:529:445:144:Times:144:Times:because  the "true" IO  account  that  separately  trace  processing  exports  and  other  
24:1286:52941:21:20:90:524:424:144:Times:122:Times:production   transactions in   national   economy   is   rarely   exist.   Fortunately, Mexico’s 
24:1287:53038:20:19:89:524:404:122:Times:122:Times:statistical  agency,  the Instituto  Nacional  de  Estadística,  Geografía  e  Informática  (INEGI),  has 
24:1288:53144:19:19:90:525:385:122:Times:122:Times:complied 2003 benchmark IO table based on economic census, which have separate accounts     for 
24:1289:53239:19:280:90:297:366:122:Times:48:Times:Mexico domestic and  Maquiladora industries8
24:1290:53283:280:7:234:237:86:144:Times:144:Times:                                                 
24:1291:53331:7:0:90:378:79:42:Times:99:Times:8 We are grateful to INEGI for providing us with the input-output table. 
24:1292:53403:0:19:297:525:366:122:Times:122:Times:, which is the major exports promotion program in 
24:1293:53453:19:19:90:525:347:122:Times:122:Times:Mexico. The table includes national production of goods and services classified under Mexico’s 
24:1294:53547:19:19:89:526:328:122:Times:122:Times:2002  3- and  4-digit  NAICS,  inputs  purchased  in  the  domestic  and Maquiladora  industries,  and  
24:1295:53651:19:20:90:532:309:122:Times:122:Times:imports  from  the  rest  of  the  world  by  both  economies.      The  domestic  and  foreign  content  share  
24:1296:53764:20:20:90:526:289:144:Times:144:Times:computed  directly  from  this  special  Mexico  IO  table provides  a  reference  benchmark  to  
24:1297:53862:20:21:90:524:269:144:Times:144:Times:test the performance of the estimation method we proposed. Based on exports and import 
24:1298:53949:21:20:90:525:248:144:Times:122:Times:statistics for Maquiladora industries in  the World Trade Atlas and Mexico's aggregate 2003 IO 
24:1299:54043:20:19:89:525:228:122:Times:122:Times:table,    we  implemented  the  same  quadratic  programming  model  that  generates  domestic/foreign  
24:1300:54147:19:19:89:526:209:122:Times:122:Times:content  estimates  for Chinese  exports,  to  compute   domestic  and  foreign  value-added  share  in  
24:1301:54252:19:19:89:525:190:122:Times:122:Times:Mexico manufacturing exports, and report the estimation results in Table 8.    The three panels in 
24:1302:54351:19:19:89:527:171:122:Times:122:Times:table  8  lists  direct/total  domestic/foreign  value-added  share  for  normal,  processing  and  total  
24:1303:54458:19:20:89:526:152:122:Times:122:Times:exports  respectively.  To  quantitatively  assess  know how  much  each  set  of  value-added  share  
24:1304:54561:20:0:89:524:132:122:Times:144:Times:estimates differs from the "true" share data computed directly from the Mexico IO table with 
25:1305:54656:0:21:90:525:709:144:Times:144:Times:a separate processing trade account, we report three type metrics in the three bottom row 
25:1306:54746:21:20:90:143:688:144:Times:122:Times:of table 8.  
25:1307:54759:20:19:125:527:668:122:Times:122:Times: The  first  bottom  row  list  the  absolute  difference  between  the  estimated  share  and  the  
25:1308:54859:19:19:89:525:649:122:Times:122:Times:"true"  shares  computed  directly  from  Mexico  IO  table  with  a  separate  processing  trade  account  
25:1309:54967:19:19:89:524:630:122:Times:122:Times:for manufacture as a whole. The errors for various share estimates seems less than 3 percentage 
25:1310:55062:19:19:89:524:611:122:Times:122:Times:point. However, it is the proportionate errors and not the absolute errors that matter; therefore, we 
25:1311:55164:19:66:89:498:592:122:Times:122:Times:computed the "Mean Absolute Percentage Error" with respect to the true shares as follows:   
25:1312:55256:66:0:230:232:526:51:Times:51:Times:i
25:1313:55257:0:25:207:211:542:51:Times:51:Times:n
25:1314:55258:25:0:205:205:517:51:Times:51:Times:=1i
25:1315:55261:0:0:255:255:560:51:Times:51:Times:ii
25:1316:55263:0:24:205:209:575:51:Times:51:Times:n
25:1317:55264:24:22:203:204:551:51:Times:51:Times:=1i
25:1318:55267:22:0:214:222:529:148:Times:148:Times: s
25:1319:55269:0:17:261:261:563:148:Times:148:Times:|s s|  100
25:1320:55279:17:17:168:123:546:148:Times:148:Times: = MAPE          
25:1321:55296:17:0:223:229:529:148:Times:148:Times:0
25:1322:55297:0:37:248:254:563:148:Times:148:Times:0
25:1323:55298:37:0:202:215:526:334:g_d0_f5:334:g_d0_f5:∑
25:1324:55299:0:14:200:234:560:334:g_d0_f5:148:g_d0_f5:∑−•
25:1325:55302:14:49:266:269:546:144:Times:144:Times: 
25:1326:55302:49:21:89:527:497:144:Times:144:Times:where  si is  the  estimated  share  and  s0i  share  is  the  reference  share for  industry  i.  The  
25:1327:55406:21:20:90:525:476:144:Times:144:Times:resulted index number is reported in the second bottom row. The error range from 4% to 
25:1328:55493:20:21:90:526:456:144:Times:144:Times:17%  for  normal  exports,  14%  to  28%  for  processing  exports  and  12%  to  15%  for  total  
25:1329:55592:21:21:90:526:435:144:Times:144:Times:exports.  Numbers  in  the  last  row  of  table  8  are  the  correlation  coefficients  between  the  
25:1330:55696:21:21:90:528:414:144:Times:144:Times:estimated  share  and  the  reference  shares,  they  reveal  that  our  estimates  are  highly  
25:1331:55793:21:19:90:527:393:144:Times:122:Times:correlated  with  the  true  shares  computed  directly  from  Mexico  IO  table  with  a  separate  
25:1332:55894:19:19:90:527:374:122:Times:122:Times:processing  trade  account  for  normal  and  total  exports,  while  the  correlation  are  lower  for  
25:1333:55999:19:30:90:178:355:122:Times:122:Times:processing exports. 
25:1334:56019:30:21:90:217:325:144:Times:144:Times:5. Concluding Remarks  
25:1335:56042:21:21:126:526:304:144:Times:144:Times: Segmentation  of  production  across  countries  allows  for  reductions  in  production  
25:1336:56132:21:20:90:527:283:144:Times:144:Times:costs  and  more  efficient  allocation  of  resources.  The  opening-up  of  China  has  likely  
25:1337:56230:20:21:89:526:263:144:Times:144:Times:facilitated  this  process.  A  quantitative  assessment  of  the  extent  of  its  participation  in  
25:1338:56333:21:21:89:527:242:144:Times:144:Times:global  production  chains  allows  us  to  get  a  better  grasp  of  many  policy  questions,  
25:1339:56430:21:20:89:454:221:144:Times:144:Times:including the effect of an exchange rate change on bilateral trade balances.  
25:1340:56507:20:21:125:526:201:144:Times:144:Times:In  this  paper,  we  first  present  a  general  framework  in  assessing  the  shares  of  
25:1341:56600:21:21:89:525:180:144:Times:144:Times:domestic  and  foreign  value  added  in  a  country’s  exports  when  tariff-favored  processing  
25:1342:56699:21:20:89:525:159:144:Times:144:Times:exports are pervasive. This formula nests the existing best known approach (HIY, 2001) 
25:1343:56786:20:21:89:525:139:144:Times:144:Times:as a special case. Because some of the I/O coefficients called for by the new formula are 
25:1344:56876:21:21:89:525:118:144:Times:144:Times:not  readily  available  from  conventional  I/O  tables,  we  propose  an  easy-to-replicate 
25:1345:56970:21:21:89:529:97:144:Times:144:Times:mathematical   programming   procedure   to   estimate   these   coefficients   by   combining   
25:1346:57067:21:0:89:530:76:144:Times:144:Times:information   from   detailed   trade   statistics   (which   records   processing   and   normal   
26:1347:57170:0:21:90:527:709:144:Times:144:Times:exports/imports  separately)  with  conventional  input-output  tables.    This  methodology  
26:1348:57264:21:21:90:527:688:144:Times:144:Times:should  be  applicable  to  Vietnam,  Mexico,  and  many  other  developing countries  that  
26:1349:57357:21:20:90:349:667:144:Times:144:Times:engage in a significant amount of processing exports. 
26:1350:57411:20:21:126:525:647:144:Times:144:Times:By  applying  our  methodology  to  Chinese  data  We find  several interesting 
26:1351:57490:21:21:90:525:626:144:Times:144:Times:patterns.  First,  the  share  of  foreign  content  in manufacturing  exports from  China  was 
26:1352:57585:21:21:90:526:605:144:Times:144:Times:close  to  50% during  1997-2002,  almost twice  as  high  as that  calculated  using the  HIY  
26:1353:57681:21:20:90:526:584:144:Times:144:Times:formula.  Second,  the  share  of  domestic  content  increased  from  51%  in  2002  to  60%  in  
26:1354:57780:20:21:90:524:564:144:Times:144:Times:2007, which corresponds to the first five years of China’s membership in the WTO. We 
26:1355:57865:21:21:90:527:543:144:Times:144:Times:also  report  interesting  heterogeneity  across  sectors:   those  sectors  that  are  likely  to  be  
26:1356:57969:21:20:90:528:522:144:Times:144:Times:labeled  as  sophisticated  or  high-skilled,  such  as  computers,  electronic  devices,  and  
26:1357:58065:20:21:90:528:502:144:Times:144:Times:telecommunication  equipment, tend  to  have  notably  low  shares  of  domestic  content.  
26:1358:58157:21:21:90:528:481:144:Times:144:Times:Conversely,  many  sectors  that  are  relatively  intensive  in  low-skilled  labor,  such  as  
26:1359:58254:21:20:90:528:460:144:Times:144:Times:apparel,  are  likely  to  exhibit  a  high  share  of  domestic  content  in  the  country’s  exports.  
26:1360:58359:20:21:90:525:440:144:Times:144:Times:Finally,  we  find  that  foreign  invested  firms  (including  both  wholly-owned  foreign  firms  
26:1361:58459:21:21:90:527:419:144:Times:144:Times:and  Sino-foreign  joint  venture  firms)  tend  to have  a  relatively  low  share  of  domestic  
26:1362:58558:21:21:90:207:398:144:Times:144:Times:content in their exports. 
26:1363:58584:21:20:126:525:377:144:Times:144:Times:There are several areas in which future research can improve upon the estimation 
26:1364:58665:20:21:90:528:357:144:Times:144:Times:in  this  paper.  First,  we  assign  initial  values  of  the  direct  domestic  value  added  for  
26:1365:58766:21:21:90:524:336:144:Times:144:Times:processing  exports  at  the  industry  level  based  on  the information  in  a  conventional  I/O 
26:1366:58866:21:20:89:525:315:144:Times:144:Times:table. If a firm-level survey data becomes available that tracks the direct value added for 
26:1367:58958:20:21:89:525:295:144:Times:144:Times:processing and normal exports separately, we can improve the accuracy of our estimates. 
26:1368:59045:21:21:90:528:274:144:Times:144:Times:Second,  as  an  inherent  limitation  of  an  I/O  table,  the  input-output  coefficients  are  
26:1369:59143:21:20:89:533:253:144:Times:144:Times:assumed to be fixed - that’s the nature of a Leontief technology -    rather than be allowed 
26:1370:59236:20:21:89:525:233:144:Times:144:Times:to  respond  to  price  changes.  This  could  be  problematic  when  a  big  change  in  export 
26:1371:59333:21:21:89:525:212:144:Times:144:Times:volume, such as what China has been experiencing, induces a change in the world market 
26:1372:59420:21:21:89:524:191:144:Times:144:Times:price  for  imported  inputs,  which  in  turn  could  trigger  a  change  in  the  underlying 
26:1373:59515:21:20:89:525:170:144:Times:144:Times:production technology and in the corresponding I/O coefficients. These could be fruitful 
26:1374:59604:20:0:89:212:150:144:Times:144:Times:areas for future research.

27:1379:59868:12:12:90:92:329:99:Times:99:Times: 
27:1380:59868:12:13:90:532:317:122:Times:122:Times:Note: “Normal  use” refers  to  “normal  exports  and  domestic  sales.”    The  UNBEC  scheme  
27:1381:59964:13:13:89:524:304:122:Times:122:Times:classifies  each  HS  6-digit  product  into  one  of  three  categories:  “intermediate  inputs,”  “capital 
27:1382:60073:13:12:89:524:291:122:Times:122:Times:goods,” and “final consumption.” For the first two categories, we further decompose the imports 
27:1383:60169:12:13:89:529:279:122:Times:122:Times:into  two  subcategories:  “processing  imports”   by  customs  declaration  are  classified  as  used  for 
27:1384:60277:13:13:89:525:266:122:Times:122:Times:producing processing  exports  and  cannot  be  sold  to  any  domestic  users  by  regulation,  and  the  
27:1385:60384:13:12:89:524:253:122:Times:122:Times:remaining imports are classified as for normal use. Capital goods are part of the final demand in a 
27:1386:60484:12:13:89:527:241:122:Times:122:Times:conventional  I/O  model  (Column  (1)  to  (5)  sum  to  100%).  However,  this  classification  may  
27:1387:60587:13:13:90:526:228:122:Times:122:Times:under-estimate  the  import  content  of  exports.  We  therefore  also  experiment  with  classifying  a  
27:1388:60694:13:12:90:526:215:122:Times:122:Times:fraction  of  the  capital  goods  as  inputs  used  in  current  year  of  production.  This  is  discussed  in  
27:1389:60808:12:0:90:145:203:122:Times:122:Times:Section 3.2.
